  <div class="layout layout--twocol-section layout--twocol-section--75-25">

          <div  class="layout__region layout__region--first">
        <section class="block block-layout-builder block-field-blocknodearticlefield-content clearfix">
  
    

      

      <div>
              <div  class="content-wrapper">
  
<script async src="https://recommend-zoom.mediacorp.sg/tag.js?network=mediacorp"></script>


<div class="text">
  

            <div class="text-long"><p>SEOUL: <span>South Korean, Chinese and Japanese leaders will hold their first trilateral summit in nearly five years next week in Seoul, South Korea's presidential office said on Thursday (May 23).</span></p>

<p><span>President Yoon Suk Yeol will meet Chinese Premier Li Qiang and Japanese Prime Minister Fumio Kishida in the South Korean capital on Monday, Seoul's deputy national security director Kim Tae-hyo told reporters.</span></p>

<p>Yoon will hold separate bilateral talks with Li and Kishida on Sunday, Kim added.</p>

<p>The three leaders are also scheduled to attend a business summit and "encourage business people from the three countries", he said.</p>

<p>The last time leaders of the three nations met was in 2019, in part due to the COVID-19 pandemic but also because of diplomatic and historical disputes between South Korea and former colonial ruler Japan.</p>

<p>Legal disputes over Japan's 1910 to 1945 rule over the Korean peninsula persist between the two countries.</p>

<p>But with <a href="https://www.channelnewsasia.com/asia/north-korea-south-korea-war-preparations-missile-inspection-russia-4336686">the increasing threat posed by nuclear-armed Pyongyang</a>, South Korea's Yoon has moved <a href="https://www.channelnewsasia.com/asia/japan-south-korea-security-defence-cooperation-thawing-relations-wwii-anniversary-3702741">to bury the historical hatchet with Japan</a>, while strengthening ties with long-standing ally Washington.</p>

<p>In August last year, Seoul, Tokyo and Washington announced a "new chapter" of close three-way security cooperation after a historic summit at Camp David in the United States.</p>

<p>At the time, Beijing lodged complaints over a statement released at the summit, in which the three allies criticised China's "aggressive behaviour" in the South China Sea.</p>

<p>Yoon last year said tensions over Taiwan were due to "attempts to change the status quo by force".</p>

<p>The announcement of the new trilateral summit came a day after Beijing reportedly summoned South Korean and Japanese diplomats to discuss "issues about Taiwan".</p>

<p>China is South Korea's biggest trade partner, but it remains North Korea's most important economic benefactor and diplomatic ally.</p>

<p>Alongside Moscow, Beijing has obstructed US-led efforts at the United Nations Security Council to impose stricter sanctions on leader Kim Jong Un's government in response to its increased weapons tests.</p>

<p>Last month, North Korean leader Kim and China's top legislator <a href="https://www.channelnewsasia.com/asia/senior-officials-stress-new-chapter-china-north-korea-ties-4262786">hailed a "new chapter"</a> of Beijing-Pyongyang relations, as the two countries celebrated 75 years of diplomatic ties.</p>

<p>The upcoming summit will mark Li's first visit to South Korea since taking office as China's premier in March 2023.<br />
 </p></div>
      
</div>
</div>
